215. I solved the 4x4x4 blindfolded!! ....... again :-)
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 20:05:28 -0000

Hey everyone, I had my second successful 4x4x4 BLD solve today. The first time I did the 4x4x4 supercube and used a completely stupid and horrible method. It took me 5 and a half hours the first time including memorization (I can't even describe how stupid and dumb my approach was when I did this two years ago). This time I wanted to try a regular 4x4x4 so that I had to choose how to cycle the centers (you have no choice for the supercube). I used the cycles method and my new and improved knowledge of commutators since the last time and successfully BLD solved a regular 4x4x4 in 1 hour 39 minutes! It took me 57 minutes to memorize and 42 to solve. Funny story actually. I meant to time the whole thing more exactly on my Stackmat (?!) but realized about 30 minutes in that the Stackmat turns off after 10 minutes ;-) I noted the time I started on my alarm clock though, so I just timed with that. The 2005 RWC really motivated me to improve my blindfolding skills (it's one of events that I really do care about that I sadly neglect the most in order to work on generic speedcubing). My goal is to do the 4x4x4 blindfolded in competition sometime soon, so I will be doing this much more often. I also want to solve the 5x5x5 (and 5x5x5 supercube eventually too) blindfolded as well. Maybe a long time from now I would want a competition 5x5 BLD solve too. One day.. Anyway many thanks to Dror, who gave me some tips for regular 4x4x4 BLD at RWC last weekend. Dror, at 2003WC you taught me how to BLD and got me addicted. Now at 2005WC you got me addicted to big cube BLD :-P Seriously though, Dror you are a huge inspiration to me, so thanks for all your help. Heh heh, well I am confident that I can BLD the 4x4x4 supercube and regular cube (regular is harder in my opinion), so now I am on to get sub-1 hour for both :-D Just wanted to share, as I was very excited to finally BLD solve the harder of the two 4x4x4 versions :-) Chris

217. Re: I solved the 4x4x4 blindfolded!! ....... again :-)
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 16:18:07 -0000

Hey Sachin, I say the 4x4x4 supercube is easier for BLD since the centers have one set cycle that you can't change. Each piece can only end up in one spot, so you just read off the cycle(s) and memorize it without doing any thinking. For regular 4x4x4 solving each center has 4 potential spots it could end up in. So you have to think about which centers to put where. Sure this can be mastered if you're someone who does big cube BLD a lot to your advantage, but it's still extra thought work and thus harder in my opinion. It's fun though! I want to get better at cycling the regular centers around :-) This big cube BLD stuff is really fun actually! Chris --- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, Sachin Shirwalkar <sachin_civilian@y...> wrote: > > Great! Congrats > > > But tell me one thing, you say twice that the 4x4x4 > normal bld is difficult that the 4x4x4 supercube bld. > hows that? or im i interpreting it wrongly? > > > Sachin. > --- cmhardw <foozman17@h...> wrote:

221. help with 4x4x4 BLD cubing
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 18:11:15 -0000

I just did a 4x4x4 BLD solve that failed. I was close except I had about 5 center pieces out of place, and 4 edge pieces. I had also undid my very last either setup move or inner layer move incorrectly, leaving an outer face almost completely solved, but off by 1 quarter turn. I've noticed that inner turns are hard to remember. Is it better to always do inner layer turns with your finger, turning just the inner layer, or the double layer followed by the outer layer? I noticed that sometimes I would do one and sometimes the other, leaving me confused as to whether I need to fix the outer layer or not (I think this is what happened with my last setup move). I think it would be best to always do it one way, what do you guys think? Also I had a question about memorizing. Since the centers require so much decision making I memorize them using numbers. However, for the edges and corners I just memorize where the pieces go. This seems to work well for me for the edges, since I can just form shapes inside the cube to follow the pieces. I did try to solve the centers just by remembering where the pieces go, but the shapes are all very skinny "X" shapes that are all the same, so it was hard and I switched to numbers. The solve would have been a 71 minute solve had I not messed up. I memorized in 31 minutes this time which was faster than my 57 from earlier. Anyway I am very serious about getting good at 4x4x4 BLD solving, and I wanted to know if any of you pro big cube solvers had any tips for anything really. I'm curious to know how you guys memorize and how you execute inner layer turns the most. I definitely use this formula for my solving A X Y X' Y' A' I have names for each part too and I say them outloud so I can remember where I am at in the commutator when cycling pieces. Since the commutators are all intuitive I find it better to use ways to not get lost than to memorize algs for specific situations. Well I'm definitely getting into this big cube BLD stuff and as a newbie I'm looking for tips :-D Thank in advance, Chris
222. Re: help with 4x4x4 BLD cubing
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 22:50:07 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > I've noticed that inner turns are hard to remember. Is it better to > always do inner layer turns with your finger, turning just the inner > layer, or the double layer followed by the outer layer? > > I noticed that sometimes I would do one and sometimes the other, > leaving me confused as to whether I need to fix the outer layer or not > (I think this is what happened with my last setup move). I think it > would be best to always do it one way, what do you guys think? YES! Not remembering whether I have to undo (Rr) or (r) has been a major pain for me in the past. So I decided to always just turn the inner layer unless I specifically want the outer layer to turn with it (in order to move a second piece at the same time which I try to avoid, though). That's the mental part. My fingers still do (r) as (Rr)R'. > I definitely use this formula for my solving > A X Y X' Y' A' Yep, that's what I do, too. I'm too lazy to learn algorithms so I rather use a very small set of commutators that I understand and can adjust on the fly, surrounded by setup moves. > I have names for each part too and I say them outloud so I can > remember where I am at in the commutator when cycling pieces. Hooray for talking to ourselves! I do it all the time, literally commenting every single turn! But I don't think Dror does, or else he must be speaking extremely fast :-) Keep us updated about your thoughts and progress! Cheers! Stefan
223. Re: help with 4x4x4 BLD cubing
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 04:07:41 -0000

Hey Stefan, I just attempted another solve and got it successfully! It took 56 minutes 53.36 seconds, which is about 42 minutes off my previous record :-D Some more comments below. > YES! Not remembering whether I have to undo (Rr) or (r) has been a > major pain for me in the past. So I decided to always just turn the > inner layer unless I specifically want the outer layer to turn with it > (in order to move a second piece at the same time which I try to > avoid, though). That's the mental part. My fingers still do (r) as > (Rr)R'. I definitely have a set standard now, and also it is thanks to your comments above. I also now only ever turn the inner layers when doing setup moves, and I do them as (Rr)R' etc.. I also like to call out my setup moves outloud so I can have some sort of auditory memory of it as well as just mental inside my head. I call inner slice turn as "little [face]" so if I had to do f2 R as a setup I would say "little f2 R" which helps me remember whether a setup turn was an inner layer or outer layer. Also I'm going to change my memorizing order, but not solving order. lately I've been memorizing corners, edges, centers and solving as corners, edges, centers. I think now I will memorize as centers, edges, corners, then solve as corners, edges, centers. I memorize the centers as numbers which is better able to withstand interference from memorizing other things to me. I'm really getting addicted to 4x4 BLD now, it's awesome! I can't wait until I've gotten a little better and it doesn't take an hour at least to do. I want to be able to do at least one solve a day. Stefan what are your times like, and how long did it take you to get there? Alright well thanks for the advice, it really helped me! Hope to be in the 30 minute or less range one day, that's my goal :-) Chris

225. more 4x4x4 BLD
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 05:13:40 -0000

Hey everyone, I just did two solves right now, both were DNF but they're getting faster. The first one was 32 minutes but I had like 8 centers out of place and 2 corners swapped. The second one was 24 minutes, but I had two centers swapped (!!!). I did (3 5 23) during center permutation instead of (3 6 23) since I am still getting used to my coordinate system. I think the secret to 4x4 BLD is to go fast and not worry about failing. I had LOTS of delays during the 24 minute solve, and I really belive that sub-10 minutes is possible with super fast memorization and break neck solving speed (as a limit to 4x4 BLD that is). I mean I'm only up to my 5th solve and I'm at 24 minutes (DNF but sitll close. If only I had done (3 6 23) aaaaaah!!!!). I really think my next successful solve will be sub-20 mins. I'm going to try to go full speed on both parts. I need to get some rest tonight, but tomorrow I will do some more solves. Maybe I am just being over ambitious, but I mean I consider myself a beginner at this, and having such a close call convincingly sub-30min solve makes me think I can go much faster. I really like memorizing as centers, edges, corners. One reason I really like this is that with careful rotation of the cube you can get up to 8 centers already solved. For both of these solves I was able to get 8 solved centers right from the start just by careful examination and rotation of the cube. So I will now memorize centers, edges, corners and solve in reverse. Also since corners are easiest you can memorize superfast and not worry about having to hold it in your head long. I can very easily see sub-20 minutes with a little more practice. Aaaah!!!! This is so addicting!!!! I'll try again tomorrow and see how it goes, wish me luck! Chris

233. Re: more 4x4x4 BLD
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 18:47:43 -0000

Hey Bernett, First off let me say that your times for BLD are very impressive! Particularly that you are so young amazes me :-) You're an inspiration to other BLD cubers like me :-) Sure I can tell you about my 4x4 BLD method, though I've just started so I don't know if it the best way to do it. The very first thing I do when the time starts is to try to rotate the cube to get as many "solved" centers as I can. I always solve the 3x3x3 BLD in the same orientation, and I use that same one for 4x4x4. I can usually get 6-8 centers solved right from the start, sometimes even as many as 9. After that I memorize the centers cycles using numbers (I'm thinking about switching to letters so I can make a story and remember it more quickly. I'll try this on my next solve). Then I memorize the edge permutation just by where the pieces go. I connect two adjacent spots in the cycle by lines in my head and follow the shapes of those lines as the cycle runs through. The corners I just use the same technique as for 3x3x3, I memorize the permutation as lines same as the edges, and orientation I just take a quick mental snapshot, since it is the first thing I solve. I use commutators and 3-cycles to solve the centers and edges, and the usual stuff from 3x3x3 supercube BLD for the corners (so I don't affect the center rotations). I'm curious how you use Stefan's method to solve the centers or edges, that is really interesting to me. How exactly do you use his idea for 4x4x4? As far as the commutators go, I mean here is an example. I just do them on the fly during a solve, I don't have any memorized algs for this. Say the first three edges of my cycle are lUB -> bUL -> rDF I need to get two of of them on the same layer and one off that layer as the setup. So I would do (L r) as my setup move. Now the cycle is uFL -> rUF -> lUB My commutator for that is X = U2 Y = B'u2B So I do XYX'Y' = (U2) (B' u2 B) (U2) (B' u2 B) then undo my setup with L' r'. I do the same type of thing for centers. Get two on the same face (anywhere) then the third center on an adjacent face. Then I just come up with a commutator that moves them. Again I don't know how efficient that is, especially the memorization. I don't claim to be any kind of memory expert, so I could probably use a lot of work on that. I'm curious what you think of my memorization technique, since you're using such a really nice system. I'd be curious what the best way to improve my memorization is. Good luck with all your future BLD efforts, and keep it up with getting those good times ;-) Chris --- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, JohnLouis Louis <pjlmem@y...> wrote: > > Hello Chris uncle, > I think , like me, you also have become an addict to BLD solving. For the last six month before wc-2005, I was practicing BLD 4*4*4 and 5*5*5. You may be learning from DNF solve. But for me it is frustrating especially when one pair of pieces are misplaced at the end. I enjoy whenever I finish correctly eventhough time taken is more. > I am following stefan's single algm method and my dad's memorisation technique. My success rate is very good now. My best time so far is 26 min 19 sec.What method you are following? Could you plz share with me uncle ? > > Bernett Orlando
234. 4x4x4 BLD memorization
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 20:14:26 -0000

Wow, so I've totally jacked the group for 4x4x4 BLD posts. I hope everyone doesn't mind :-S Anyway I've been thinking about memorization for the 4x4x4 centers, and though I probably should use letters and form words, I really like working with numbers. I can use operators like addition subtraction, things like prime numbers, divsors, etc. to form relations between consecutive numbers. I've found that I memorize quickest to learn 4 pieces in a cycle, then take time to remember them, then do 4 more pieces. If there aren't 4 to end the cycle then I just do the last amount. I also really like just remember where edges go, so I don't have two sets of numbers, of I prefer this to letters since it is easy for me to just remember where they move. I just got a new pb solve of 26 minutes 4.60 seconds successfully! I know I can still go much faster with my method, but I need to work on speeding up my solve and memorization. For the 26 minute solve I memorized in about 13:40 and solved in about 12:24 so my individual steps are getting faster. I've noticed that it really helps me to just not worry about whether or not the solve is a DNF or not. If I worry, I will usually get nervous and confuse whether or not I need to finish with a slice turn or an edge insert step for my commutators and just mess everything up. It's better to just trust your memory and visualizing of where the pieces are and to just solve. Well, I guess I'll quiet down for a while, now that I am getting a better success rate and better times I just need to practice more. I do hope for sub-20 minutes soon though :-) Thanks everyone for the help, this group is awesome ;-D Chris
235. _Not_ a 4x4x4 BLD thread :)
From: "thomkirjava" <snkenjoi@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 23:13:08 -0000

Time to take things back to the land of the sane.... :P Just scored a sweet 4:56.54 BLD solve. My new PB. I wrote down the solution I used, dunno if this would be of interest to anyone. Sub-5mins! Yay! I'm usually around the 5-6 mark, but it's good to break 5. Top - Red, Front - White Scramble; DUB2D2B2F2R2FL'U'R2B'R2DB2UL2F'U'F'U'D'F2D'B2 Solution; Corner Orientation: y(RUR'URU2R'L'U'LU'L'U2L)y' x2(RUR'URU2R'L'U'LU'L'U2L)x2 x'y(RUR'URU2R'L'U'LU'L'U2L)y'x Corner Permutation: (D'R2D2B2)(RB'RF2R'BRF2R2)(B2D2R2D) (B2DB2)(RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')(B2D'B2) (D'B2)(RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')(B2D) Edges: L(RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')L' (D'l')(L'URU'LU2'R'URU2R')(lD) (RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')(LU'R'UL'U2'RU'R'U2R) (d'L')(RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')(Ld) (RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F') (L'URU'LU2'R'URU2R') (dL)(RUR'U'R'FR2U'R'U'RUR'F')(L'd') l'(L'URU'LU2'R'URU2R')l (L'URU'LU2'R'URU2R') This is probibly horrible for any of you genius BLD'rs, but I shall learn from mistakes. New algs ahoy! ~Thom

Il me semble que les jeunes se rangent peu à peu avec moi quand je vais sur les forums. Quand je verrai mon lien sur les engish webmaster comme Stefan, Macky, Andy, Bob or many other excellent cuber disons 1/5, j'irai au WC 2007. Sinon enlevez mon adresse. Le cube n'a pas la noblesse ni la richesse de la chess game mais il est merveilleux. Vous avez une méthode alors vous êtes déjà un magicien et personne ne sait que vos centres ont tournées sur eux- mêmes, vous devriez avoir honte de cacher mon nom. The old boss at the WCA and the young Tyson, imagine my trick at your city (priority on the others) in 1993 not 2005! For your friend, Akimoto I tooked this link a long time ago, me! He proposed to me without I asking it to him. I know and him too !. Tu merites plus d'honneurs. Pour ton système et pour ta magie » (Ron van Bruchem). ID: ilovemycube Hobbies: Rubiks Cube, Numbers, Magic tricks, Othello/Reversi, Programming, Darts My personnal best unofficial record....................................... http://grrroux.free.fr French cuber !!! Incredible! I'm french too. I tooked this link along time ago not him. I request a minimum not a favorite link !!! Do you see many good french website with the cube. J'ai cru entendre dire par Lars P. que sa méthode est inutilement complexe. Si vous aimez l'usage élégante de M par U alors imaginez combien une méthode 2x2x2 demande le M avec le cube. Finally, at the third point of the triangle there is the Instrument of Betrayal. This is the person who apparently enters an already existing relationship between two people and threatens to destroy or change it. This point of the triangle usually gets a rather bad press, being seen as "predatory" or a taker of someone else's beloved possession. If we happen to occupy this point, we may receive only limited sympathy, and none at all from those in established relationships who feel the cold wind (boss wca) of their own possible future.. In fact, the Instrument of Betrayal may feel himself or herself to be a victim, and may perceive the Betrayed as the predator. We can begin to glimpse the secret identity between these two points of the triangle (Liz Greene). I respect the WCA but him disrespect my difference. N'attendez pas mon retour avec 3 master de la chess game + one grand master car il vous feront honte à mon avantage. Ils attendent votre réaction. Un pour tous et tous pour un et le cube sera encore plus populaire, vous n'avez rien vu. Oui je suis un speedcuber blindfold mais ma magie devrait suffire à vos esprits enfermer dans une intelligence uniquement logique avec un cube. Les animaux sont plus intelligent que nous L'humain recherche trop le pouvoir et il détruit la planète, il est le plus grand microbe car il veut copier se que le nature fait d'elle-même, il va payer le prix. Einstein avait raison l'imagination dépasse l'intelligence. Il était un scientifique mais il a une perception comme M.Rubik car je pense que vous ne voyez que la performance de vos records. Allons voyons il y a tellement de variété de record avec le cube et il ne sera jamais poupulaire autant que la chess game. Ce n'est pas la publicité et les championnats qui ont vendu le cube à ses débuts, sa vente a été magique. Ne croyez-vous pas qu'il serait bon de parler d'un cubiste magique ou d'une différence. Pourquoi faire voir toujours les mêmes noms et les mêmes choses ? Dror Vomberg was not even a twinkle in his mother's eye during the Rubik's ...He once saw a man doing the puzzle behind his back and was inspired to try. "I thought this guy has to have extraordinary vision or something," he said. "I thought I'd try it." http://www.cjnews.com/viewarticle.asp?id=1499 No, no no and one more time........ Cube day 2002 and celebration 1980-2005, puplicity tv, unique master piece. http://www.rubikscuberecord.com/film.wmv (internet high speed only) impossible download. Je suis capable de résoudre le cube pendant que je multiplie des gros nombres. Je ne suis pas seulement un magicien du cube. Anyway I had a official paper Guinness. Que je place une vieille vidéo de moi « one hand » 1983-84 et un cube en moins de 20 secondes bientôt et que je vous prouve que je suis un speedcuber blindfold ne changera rien car mon site a le minimum d'être vu par tous par sa différence. Ne vous noyez pas dans un esprit snobe à cause de votre inconscience et l'influence des vieux se temps est fini. Gaétan

249. just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 22 Nov 2005 23:41:09 -0000

If you know my blindfold method then you know I'm solving pieces one by one, swapping two pieces. But I also swap two certain pieces of the other type (edges or corners) as an annoying unwanted "side effect" because I have to. Well, that's what I've thought until this weekend. Here's how to swap the edges UR<->LU without changing any other edges or corners: R E R D2 R' E' R D2 R2 S This is the first algorithm I came up with, I could imagine there are shorter/faster ones. Can someone find a better one? How about one for corners? No idea how practical this could be but I like it a lot from a theoretical point of view so I thought I'd mention it. Cheers! Stefan
250. Re: [blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube] just swapping 2 pieces
From: Michael Zener Riggs Gottlieb <mzrg@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 22 Nov 2005 19:08:34 -0500

> R E R D2 R' E' R D2 R2 S > This is the first algorithm I came up with, I could imagine there are > shorter/faster ones. Can someone find a better one? How about one for > corners? > No idea how practical this could be but I like it a lot from a > theoretical point of view so I thought I'd mention it. > Cheers! > Stefan Looks like a good idea, but wouldn't that make it so you'd have to remember the locations of the centers as well? By doing that, you might end up with a 6-spot configuration if you aren't extremely careful. --qqwref
251. Re: just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 23 Nov 2005 01:01:11 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, Michael Zener Riggs Gottlieb <mzrg@v...> wrote: > > > R E R D2 R' E' R D2 R2 S > > This is the first algorithm I came up with, I could imagine there are > > shorter/faster ones. Can someone find a better one? How about one for > > corners? > > No idea how practical this could be but I like it a lot from a > > theoretical point of view so I thought I'd mention it. > > Cheers! > > Stefan > > Looks like a good idea, but wouldn't that make it so you'd have to remember > the locations of the centers as well? By doing that, you might end up with a > 6-spot configuration if you aren't extremely careful. No, I'd only use algorithms that rotate the centers in one slice and in one direction, e.g. always only the S-slice in the direction of an S-turn. Then after solving all edges and corners, the cube is either solved or you need to add e.g. (M2 S M2 S'). To determine whether you have to do that, count the number of steps modulo 4. Alternatively, you could have two algorithms for each case, one that rotates the centers in one direction, one for the other direction. Then start with the centers solved and alternate the direction of the center rotations by choosing the appropriate algs. Hey, I just noticed another advantage of this. It pretty much gives you four cube orientations to choose from for free. For example, if you solve so that yellow ends up on top and orange on front, you can in the beginning orient the cube as a whole so that the yellow center is on top and the orange is on front. But you can just as well rotate the whole cube around the z-axis so that the yellow center is on R, D or L. Just pick the one that looks easiest to solve (e.g. most edges and corners already solved or fewest correctly placed but with bad orientation). Cheers! Stefan
252. Re: just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 23 Nov 2005 01:25:48 -0000

HAHAHAHAHA!!! I found it! The holy grail for everybody who hates the usual parity problem! Instead of my previously shown alg, try this one: R E R D2 R' E' R D2 R2 S2 E S' E' Using this you can completely absolutely 100% *ignore* the parity "problem"! You don't need to care about it - at all! Thanks Michael for your question, maybe I wouldn't have thought about this without it. Uh, I gotta award myself for this now. Wanted to go to bed but now I'm gonna watch two Cheers episodes :-) Cheers! 257. Re: just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 23 Nov 2005 16:26:19 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, Michael Zener Riggs Gottlieb <mzrg@v...> wrote: > > > P.S. currently use the cycle method, but im going to look into your > > method once my exam ends. > > Sachin. > > Ah, but with this one, it switches the centers in 2-cycles. Since you'll > have to do it an even number of times anyway (by parity), as long as you > keep the cube in the same orientation every time you do this alg, you'll > have absolutely nothing to worry about. Yep, that's the idea. You start with the centers correct and will automatically end up with them correct again. I played a bit with ACube and came up with this algorithm which is I think faster: U L' R D F U r' B' U R U' R' U' r' d' R It also swaps two "diagonally opposite" edges (UB<->DF), which is better because it'll make setup moves shorter. I just need one more that swaps (UB<->FD) and then the average number of setup moves for edges will be (2*0+12*1+8*2)/22 = 1.27 moves. And then a similar algorithm for corners, i.e. that swaps the centers the same way and swaps two diagonally opposite corners, resulting in (1*0+9*1+11*2)/21 = 1.41 setup moves on average for corners. Adding two more for the other orientations of the corners would even drop this average to (3*0+18*1)/21 = 0.86 moves. Btw, Sachin, my method is also a cycle method. Just probably in smaller steps than you're currently used to. Cheers! Stefan
258. Re: just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 23 Nov 2005 16:31:47 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, Pedro <pedrosino1@y...> wrote: > > If I did the alg correctly, the UR and UL edges are flipped and swapped. To my mind, they're not flipped. They're only swapped. The idea of "flipped" edges for me only exists for edges that are at the correct place. The algorithm I showed simply swaps UR and LU (or equivalently you can think of it as swapping RU and UL). > So, how is this thing useful? You correct the parity but change the centers... This is not intended to correct the parity. With this idea, you don't care about parity issues at all. Overall, for solving all edges and all corners, you'll always need an even number of swaps of two pieces. Now do the algorithm twice and look what happens. The cube will be solved again. So yes, after an odd number of swaps the centers will be out of place, but after an even number of swaps they'll be in place again, particularly at the very end of the solve. > and where's the similar alg for the corners? I'm working on it :-) Cheers! Stefan

262. Re: just swapping 2 pieces
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Wed, 23 Nov 2005 18:41:13 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@g...> wrote: > > > and where's the similar alg for the corners? > > I'm working on it :-) Ok, here's one for corners: D L B L' U' F' L B D B' U' B L2 F' R' D r2 u D And here's a corresponding one (i.e. same center swaps) for edges again: U L' R D F U r' B' U R U' R' U' r' d' R I didn't let ACube finish the computations and I had to integrate the center rotations by hand and didn't spend much time on it so there are almost certainly better algs for the same effects. Also, I'd prefer to use the DB edge and the DBL corner as buffer pieces and as targets the UF edge and URF corner places with all their orientations. Then setup moves for the corners would only be an U, R or F turn, and setup moves for the edges would usually be an F or U turn, sometimes with an L or R turn beforehand. Quick summary for the method: - 5 algs to learn - on average 1.07 setup turns, worst case 2 quarter turns - setup turns only in <U,R,F,L> - ignore parity Cheers! Stefan

Yeah, that's the main reason I said "No idea how practical this could be but I like it a lot from a theoretical point of view". I wish ACube could search with double-layer twists and moving centers and I wish my computer were fast enough to complete a search in less than let's say an hour. Then maybe we could find nice optimal algs in for example <U,R,F,u,r,f>. But I've already let it search with all six sides allowed to turn and I stopped it at I think 17 QTM and 15 HTM, so those are lower bounds and they're quite high, too high to win against my current method whose only disadvantage is that I can't completely ignore the parity issue but have to do an easy check and fix. Cheers! Stefan

267. 4x4x4 BLD memorization
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 25 Nov 2005 00:19:39 -0000

Not to beat this into the ground, but I wanted to ask about something. I remember J. Bernett Orlando and Stefan using nouns and images together to make a story for memorization. I use this technique whenever I have to memorize a list, or a sequence of things in the real world. I find it odd that I never thought to do this for the 4x4x4. I just came up with 24 nouns and have just finished memorizing the new scheme (I used to use numbers). I just did my first centers solve successfully with the new memorization technique, so now I'm ready to do a full solve. Anyway, I have a feeling this will be much faster than the numbers scheme I used to use, since I tailored my nouns to easily be able to make really funny/silly stories which makes it easier to memorize. Alright, well I was just curious what others thought about nouns vs. numbers. I definitely seem to prefer nouns now. Chris

271. Re: [blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube] Re: 4x4x4 BLD memorization
From: Michael Zener Riggs Gottlieb <mzrg@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 25 Nov 2005 13:13:24 -0500

A while ago I found that (M' U)*4 is a pretty good tool for edge flips. It flips UL, UB, DF, and DB. If you do ((M' U)*4 + [clockwise 120-degree rotation through FLU/BRD axis])*3, you get the superflip. If you do (M' U)*3 M' U2 (M' U)*3 M', you flip UF and UB. If you do (M' U)*3 M' U' (M' U)*3 M' U', as stated before by Pedro, you flip UF, UL, UR, and UB. If you do (M' U)*4 z2 (M' U)*4 z2, you again flip UF, UL, UR, and UB. Pretty versatile, if you ask me. :-) The only thing it doesn't really like to do is flip two *adjacent* edges. For example: if you do z2 (M' U)*4 x2 (M' U)*3 M' U2 (M' U)*3 M' x2 z2, you can flip UF and UR. --qqwref

I feel that I am learning new things every time, and that eventually I will be able to do this without DNF'ing so often. Has anyone else taken so incredibly long to get used to 4x4 BLD? I'm not trying to be careful, but rather to go fast and get a good time. I want to get my brain used to this speed, rather than going slow and just getting a solve but taking almost half again as long to do it. So far my story method for the centers allows me to do one time through memorizing, since it's easy for my brain to remember a story compared to a sequence of numbers. I very consistently memorize in 11-14 minutes and the whole solve (if they weren't DNFs) take me about 21-24 minutes. I'm not going to give up on this, but man oh man is it hard to learn how to do. I've started taking pictures of my solves, and on the last one I messed up the corners step and had two centers swapped in the end. I'm going to keep taking pictures to hopefully learn more. Can't wait to get over the learning curve and start getting fast successful solves. Hey all you other 4x4 BLDers how is your progress going? I need some encouragement lol, is anyone else going through this too, or am I just a slow learner like usual? ;-) Chris
278. An example 4x4x4 BLD solve (by request)
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 26 Nov 2005 07:07:07 -0000

Hey everyone, I finally got another 4x4 BLD solve successfully. It's actually my new record at 24 minutes 10.61 seconds. I decided to go a bit slower than I had been going on memorization, but still go full speed on the solving. Anyway, I had gotten some requests for a sample 4x4x4 BLD solve, and I wanted to wait until I got a successful one so I could talk about it practically, rather than in theory. Here's the scramble: F R' b2 L2 r' B2 R' L' F' U' b d f2 d' B' R' u R2 b u2 F' l L f B' D U' r2 F2 L u2 b r2 u2 B' R d' f' B' d The first thing I do is to get as many centers solved as I can. My color scheme that I solve to is yellow on top and green on front. Do the rotation z right now (rotate the whole cube as if you're doing the move F). This gets 7 centers solved right off the bat. Ok now I have to memorize the centers. The cycle I used is (lbU -> ruF -> rbU -> buL -> lfU -> brD -> dbL -> ufR -> blD -> frU - > frD -> ubR -> fdL -> lfD -> ruB -> dlF -> luB) The notation means the only piece on the intersection of the three slices named. The piece lbU is the only piece on the intersection of "l" "b" and "U". I have names for each spot, using the name my list is (Larry -> airplane -> Batman -> Giraffe -> the Terminator -> Book -> Alligator -> the South Pole -> sword -> Spiderman -> rubber duckie - > Classroom/Lecture Hall -> hamster -> chair -> skydiving -> the back to the future III train time machine -> mountaineering) And the story I made up is: LARRY is the pilot of an AIRPLANE and accidently flies it into BATMAN, who was in freefall in the air. Meanwhile, below the plane accident, a GIRAFFE is hunting the TERMINATOR, who is reading a BOOK with a picture of an ALLIGATOR on it. The Giraffe kicks the Terminator to the SOUTH POLE. Once he gets his bearings straight the Terminator draws a SWORD to do battle with SPIDERMAN, who unfortunately is only armed with a RUBBER DUCKIE. This pans out to a CLASSROOM where the students were watching this on a discovery channel episode. Suddenly a giant HAMSTER rips through the roof and starts ripping apart the classroom and CHAIRs are flying everywhere. Meanwhile, above, a SKYDIVER in midair falls into the wood storage car of the BACK TO THE FUTURE TRAIN TIME MACHINE. Just when he realizes where he is the time machine flies into a MOUNTAIN and explodes. I know the story is really dumb and silly, but that is exactly why it is easy to remember. I read a lot about memory, and one of the techniques is not only to make a story silly, but also to try to make it shocking. That's why I have the train explode, and the hamster destroy the classroom with students in it. It's sound weird, but the technique says that whatever makes you laugh, or shocks you, is easier to remember. Ok, so those are the centers. The edges cycle as: (lUB -> fUR -> uFL -> dFR -> uBL -> dBL -> fDL -> rFU -> uBR -> bDL - > rFD -> rBU -> dBR -> lBD -> dFL -> lFD -> fUL -> bDR -> bUR -> rBD -> fDR) For the edges I just memorize where they go. I try to picture it in my head as one piece that moves through each of these locations, and I picture the intermittent moves sometimes as well, whatever helps. The corners cycle as (UBL -> DFL -> UBR) and (UFL -> DBR -> UFR) and (DBL -> DFR) and they flip as UBL needs to flip clockwise and DFL needs to flip counterclockwise. Ok here's the solve: ----------------------------------- First I solve corner orientation, since it's the last thing I memorize and I can just take a quick snapshot of it if I solve it first. To solve I did U' x R' U' R U' R' U2 R L U L' U L U2 L' x' U (x is the rotation that means to turn your whole cube as if you were doing the move R, x' is like R') Now I do corner permutation (UBL -> DFL -> UBR) F2 R2 B2 R F R' B2 R F' R F2 (UFL -> DBR -> UFR) B2 F2 L2 F' R' F L2 F' R F' B2 (DBL -> DFR) For this I can't solve them yet, since any alg that moves just two corners must also perform an odd cycle somewhere on the centers (think 4x4x4 supercube). Instead I just want to get them ready to solve later. F L' F' L F L' F' L F L' F' L - F' L F L' F' L F L' F' L F L' - R2 B2 R F R' B2 R F' R I'm sure there is a better way to do this, but with the clock ticking and me wanting to use center safe algs this is how I did it. I end up with the corner cycle (UBL <-> UBR). EDGES: ------------------------------------ Here all I use are commutators, I have absolutely no memorized algs for any sort of cycles. (lUB -> fUR -> uFL -> dFR -> uBL -> dBL -> fDL -> rFU -> uBR -> bDL - > rFD -> rBU -> dBR -> lBD -> dFL -> lFD -> fUL -> bDR -> bUR -> rBD -> fDR) Here are the commutators I used. I will only write them as [X,Y] which means to do the permutation X Y X' Y' I'll write setup moves around the commutator notation as well. (lUB -> fUR -> uFL) = f' [B' u2 B, U] f Ok, so to make sure things are clear X=(B' u2 B) and Y=(U) so f' [B' u2 B, U] f = f' B' u2 B U B' u2 B U' f (lUB -> dFR -> uBL) = L [U, B d2 B'] L' again just to help clarify L [U, B d2 B'] L' = L U B d2 B' U' B d2 B' L' (lUB -> dBL -> fDL) = [L', D' l' D] (lUB -> rFU -> uBR) = [U2, F' u2 F] (lUB -> bDL -> rFD) = L2 D2 [B d B', U] D2 L2 (lUB -> rBU -> dBR) = r' [U2, F d' F'] r (lUB -> lBD -> dFL) = L' [U, B d B'] L (lUB -> lFD -> fUL) = F' [L d' L', U'] F (lUB -> bDR -> bUR) = [R d R', U] (lUB -> rBD -> fDR) = U' L [D', R' d2 R] L' U And now the edges are solved. CENTERS: ------------------------------------- Same as the edges I have no memorized algs for this. I solve this entirely using commutators. I'll use the same [X,Y] notation here as above. (lbU -> ruF -> rbU -> buL -> lfU -> brD -> dbL -> ufR -> blD -> frU - > frD -> ubR -> fdL -> lfD -> ruB -> dlF -> luB) (lbU -> ruF -> rbU) = [U', b' u' b] (lbU -> buL -> lfU) = [U, l u' l'] (lbU -> brD -> dbL) = r2 [U2, f d2 f'] r2 (lbU -> ufR -> blD) = D2 f' [l u l', U] f D2 (lbU -> frU -> frD) = r F' r' [U2, r u2 r'] r F r' (lbU -> ubR -> fdL) = f [l' u' l, U'] f' (lbU -> lfD -> ruB) = D2 r' [U2, l u2 l'] r D2 (lbU -> dlF -> luB) = F2 r [U, r' u2 r] r' F2 ------------------------ FINISHING: Ok now we have to finish off our corners. To do this swap two edges, then end like a 3x3x3. (Uu)2 (Ll)2 U2 l2 U2 (Ll)2 (Uu)2 y' L' U' L U L F' L2 U L U L' U' L F And now the cube is solved. I realize that the centers can be done more efficiently, but I am taking Dror's advice that he gave me at RWC2005 to try to put the centers into one long cycle to help with memorization. I may try to optimize them later, but for now I like making one long cycle to ease the memorization. Anyway there is an example solve, let me know if you have any questions. This solve is not theory, but is actually a reconstruction of my current record solve. Hope this helps, Chris

287. Re: Sub-20!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 26 Nov 2005 23:59:22 -0000

Hey Stefan, > Hi Chris, > > congrats, that's awesome! When are you going to attack the 5x5? Thanks, though I do think your official competition 5x5 solve is much more impressive ;-) I want to tackle the 5x5x5 very soon, but I want to wait until I have a better success rate for the 4x4x4. I already have all the algs ready that I will use for the 5x5x5 (the central edges and such) and I know how I will memorize. I just need to be more used to working my brain that hard. I have a feeling a 5x5x5 DNF is much more of a downer than a 4x4 DNF. > Thanks for your replay of your 4x4 solve, I didn't actually execute it > but I read over it and I like your analysis. Will have to look at your > single long center cycle again. The centers are for me the hardest > part of large cube blindsolving. I have huge trouble planning what > shall go where, keeping track of what I decided for yet. How do you do > this? As far as memorizaing the centers, in order to try to make the longest cycles possible I have an order of importance on each face that is based off my supercube 4x4 numbering. Each face has the centers labeled in decreasing priority. So there is a 1st priority spot, a 2nd priority spot, third, and fourth. When I run into say a red center in my cycle, I cycle it to the highest available priority spot on the red face. When I have placed a piece into the lowest priority spot I remember that the red face say is "full", since I would have filled all the other spots before the 4th one. When a cycle ends sooner, and I have remaining pieces, I just think of the faces where I haven't hit the 4th priority spot and start there. In terms of my story method I know that Spiderman, the Batmobile, Germany, a rubik's cube competition, a giant hamster, and a chair are all my 4th priority locations. If a cycle ends too soon, I review my story to see if I don't have any of these 4th priority things in it. The one I don't have is the face I check first when starting my other cycle. Hope that helps, Chris P.S. Now that I have more practice with blindfolded larger-than-the- 3x3x3-cube-stuff I think you're absolutely insane to attempt the megaminx, and even more impressive to actually get it!! Now that I have more of an idea what that must involve, I think it is absolutely amazing! --- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@g...> wrote: > > Hi Chris, > > congrats, that's awesome! When are you going to attack the 5x5? > > Thanks for your replay of your 4x4 solve, I didn't actually execute it > but I read over it and I like your analysis. Will have to look at your > single long center cycle again. The centers are for me the hardest > part of large cube blindsolving. I have huge trouble planning what > shall go where, keeping track of what I decided for yet. How do you do > this? > > Cheers! > Stefan

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > Thanks, though I do think your official competition 5x5 solve is > much more impressive ;-) Hmm, not necessarily to me... when I first started blindsolving and was very happy getting the 2x2 in a little over 20 minutes, I was still amazed by the large cube blindsolving others have done. Later when I learned more and was placed very high in the "amazing blindfold achievements" category (which doesn't exist anymore) I felt that name was wrong. Nothing in there really amazed me anymore. Like, would you be amazed by a 15 seconds 3x3 speedsolve? No, you know how it's done and it has become normal. Anybody can blindsolve, including larger cubes. But I'm still very much impressed by the speed some of you are showing. > I have a feeling a 5x5x5 DNF is much > more of a downer than a 4x4 DNF. Maybe it's not, because your expectation to get it right is smaller : -) > As far as memorizaing the centers, in order to try to make the > longest cycles possible I have an order of importance on each face > that is based off my supercube 4x4 numbering. Each face has the > centers labeled in decreasing priority. So there is a 1st priority > spot, a 2nd priority spot, third, and fourth. When I run into say a > red center in my cycle, I cycle it to the highest available priority > spot on the red face. When I have placed a piece into the lowest > priority spot I remember that the red face say is "full", since I > would have filled all the other spots before the 4th one. When a > cycle ends sooner, and I have remaining pieces, I just think of the > faces where I haven't hit the 4th priority spot and start there. Ok, thanks. That's similar to what I've done, only that I'm using my fingers to tell me where in a face I am. That is, I mainly hold the cube with three fingers of my left hand and three of my right hand (thumb, index and ring finger, cause I can spread those the most). The other fingers stabilize the cube and are not allowed to touch the pieces I'm analyzing so I don't get confused because of them. Of course I can't let go, put the cube down and pick it up again, without getting confused :-). How do you know at what spot you are in a certain face? Do you just have a feeling which nouns you've already used or do you replay the story to look for them? > P.S. Now that I have more practice with blindfolded larger-than-the- > 3x3x3-cube-stuff I think you're absolutely insane to attempt the > megaminx, and even more impressive to actually get it!! Now that I > have more of an idea what that must involve, I think it is > absolutely amazing! Well, let me compare 4x4 and Megaminx: - Megaminx has 50 moving pieces, 4x4 has 56, make that 50 because you can get some centers for free. So about the same number of pieces to solve. - Megaminx has no parity problems because each fifth turn of a face is a 5-cycle of edges and corners, i.e. an even permutation. - Megaminx tells you exactly where everything goes, 4x4 you must decide and keep track where the centers go, very hard for me. - Megaminx has long setup moves because it just takes long to get a piece from here to there. On the other hand, it gives you a lot of freedom for setting up two pieces of a 3-cycle independently. The 4x4 has short setup moves, though setting up the edges can be annoying, especially if you want to for example bring UFr to UFl. - Megaminx has more colors (12 instead of 6) and more color pairs (60 instead of 24) so you need a larger pool of nouns or whatever. But you can make them up on the fly. For example, I encoded the white/purple edge as a mental image of a WhaLe, because W=white and L=Lila (German for purple). Overall I think Megaminx might be a bit harder than 4x4, but I think it's easier than 5x5. And you'll get that one soon, too. And then the Megaminx. And then we can race for Dogic :-). Or, well, just choose the route you like. I know I went straight from 3x3 to Megaminx because I wanted to be the first to do it and 4x4 and 5x5 had been done already. Cheers! Stefan
289. Re: Sub-20!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 27 Nov 2005 04:15:21 -0000

> Ok, thanks. That's similar to what I've done, only that I'm using my > fingers to tell me where in a face I am. That is, I mainly hold the > cube with three fingers of my left hand and three of my right hand > (thumb, index and ring finger, cause I can spread those the most). The > other fingers stabilize the cube and are not allowed to touch the > pieces I'm analyzing so I don't get confused because of them. Of > course I can't let go, put the cube down and pick it up again, without > getting confused :-). How do you know at what spot you are in a > certain face? Do you just have a feeling which nouns you've already > used or do you replay the story to look for them? When I was using numbers I had groups of 4 numbers, and when I hit a face again, I tried to think which of the numbers in that group I had already used. This can be slow sometimes, which is why I switched to nouns. I group the nouns by category on each face. Also, here are my priorities: U Face (People) 1) Larry (any random person) - lbU 2) Batman - rbU 3) the Terminator - lfU 4) Spiderman - rfU F face (modes of transportation) 1) Bus - luF 2) Airplane - ruF 3) back to the future III train time machine - dlF 4) the Batmobile - drF R face (places) 1) the south pole - ufR 2) a classroom/lecture hall - ubR 3) the neighborhood I grew up in - dfR 4) Germany - dbR B face (actions) 1) skydiving - urB 2) mountaineering - ulB 3) competiting in the Ironman triathlon - drB 4) competing in a rubik's cube competition - dlB L face (animals) 1) Giraffe - ubL 2) Zebra - ufL 3) Alligator - dbL 4) giant hamster - dfL D face (things) 1) book - rbD 2) knife/sword - lbD 3) rubber duckie - rfD 4) chair - lfD When I'm in the middle of a cycle and I have a piece cycle to say the L face, then I think of the most recent animal in my story. If I can remember a zebra and alligator is not solved then I know I have alligator next. If I can remember alligator, then I know giant hamster is next. So I don't even have to use my fingers to mark the ones on each face that I have used last, I just figure it out based on the category of that face. Now when I see a red center I know it is an animal, an orange is a place, etc.. Also, I tried to craft my nouns to be able to be silly (giant hamster, comic book heroes, train time machine, etc.) and also shocking (terminator, mountaineering which can be dangerous, sword, etc.) > Overall I think Megaminx might be a bit harder than 4x4, but I think > it's easier than 5x5. And you'll get that one soon, too. And then the > Megaminx. And then we can race for Dogic :-). Or, well, just choose > the route you like. I know I went straight from 3x3 to Megaminx > because I wanted to be the first to do it and 4x4 and 5x5 had been > done already. I guess one day I'l try the megaminx, but I am still very much intimidated by it. I want to try to get faster and more consistent with the 4x4x4, then probably after I graduate in December and have lots of free time to get addicted to 5x5x5 BLD I will try it. I guess my goals are not so much to do lots of things blindfolded, but to get fast at doing the puzzles I choose to do, which are mainly 4x4x4 and hopefully one day 5x5x5. I do also, though, want to be able to claim the 6x6x6 BLD. I doubt I will beat you to it, but one day I want that to be on my cubing resume so to speak ;-) Chris > > Cheers! > Stefan >

294. How come we let the cube decide... ?
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 28 Nov 2005 08:12:43 -0000

I always solve so that yellow ends up on top and orange on front. So first thing I do with the scrambled 3x3 is to rotate the cube as a whole such that the orange center is on front and the yellow center is on top. But why? There are 11 other cube orientations that I could easily choose from. For example, I could start with F=white and U=green. Then the first thing I'd do after blindfolding is apply E'M'EM. This will make F=orange and U=yellow without changing any edges or corners. Of course there are 24 cube orientations overall, but half of them can't be fixed like that without changing edges and corners. And 1 is the "correct" orientation and the other 11 can all be fixed with algs in <M,E> like these and their mirrors: E' M' E M M2 E M2 E' M' E M2 E' M' For my own method I don't think it'll be a big advantage, though I'll think about that again. But for the 4-step/3-cycle guys like Tyson&Co I could imagine this to be helpful, for example like this: 1) orient cube to maximize white/yellow stickers on U/D (i.e. maximize correctly oriented corners) 2) turn cube upside down if that brings more corners into their correct layer (if that's helpful for you, don't know) 3) do y if necessary to reach one of the 12 "good" orientations 4) do y2 if that solves more corners What do you (especially Tyson&Co) think about this? We shouldn't let the cube dictate its orientation to us. We should exploit easier cases among the other 11 possibilities. Cheers! Stefan

300. Re: How come we let the cube decide... ?
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 28 Nov 2005 21:53:04 -0000

--- In blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > Well, I'm no Tyson or Leyan, but I definitely try to be. Yeah, mainly I just meant everybody who orients and permutes separately. > Actually finding the E M E' M' is what took me the longest for fixing > the centers Hehe, that's supposed to be an easy task :-) (M2 E M2 E') and (E2 M E2 M') are I guess easiest to understand. (M E M2 E' M) is just a single case and built from (M2 E M2 E'). I think about the eight variants of (E M E' M') like this: - First move just brings correct center to front. - Fourth move shall bring original F center to its goal, so the second move must go in the other direction. It also preserves the correct F center by letting it step aside for a moment. - Undo first move, this brings the original F center back to F. - Undo second move, the correct F center steps back to F, and the original F center moves to its goal face. You oughta solve Cmetrick to practice this :-) Cheers! Stefan
301. Re: How come we let the cube decide... ?
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 28 Nov 2005 22:46:49 -0000

Hey Stefan, I thought of a way to do this but use less center algs. I track the red, green, and yellow centers. Imagine the 3 of them like a 2x2x2 inside the 3x3x3. This red-green-yellow 2x2x2 can only be in the top two layers or the bottom two layers. If it is in the top two layers I use a y rotation to get it to the FL edge. Same for if it is in the D layer. This 2x2x2 can only be in the u layer at FL or FR or the d layer at FR and BL. So why not always rotate it to the same spot? This saves you from having to know 4 more algs, plus it would speed up memorization, having less possible cases. Also a y rotation won't affect corner orientation. Or you could even use the y2 rotation to optimize the corner permutation as well. Who knows, this can go lots of different ways. I am inclined to think that always rotating the 2x2x2 to the FL edge would make the memorization much easier, and thus really make the time spent optimizing corner orientation not time lost in vain. Open to new ideas, but I definitely want to try putting the 2x2x2 on FL always. This leaves only 8 cases including the solved case for the centers. What do you think? 302. algs for moving centers
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 28 Nov 2005 23:15:39 -0000

Hey Stefan and others, Actually all the cases for moving centers are really easy commutators. I don't even think you would need to rotate U to put the 2x2x2 in the same spot, you can just use these. ok, so the 2x2x2 that belongs in uFL is the one I am talking about. It can be in either uFL, uBR, dFR, dBL for me. If you choose another one it can be in the other locations not mentioned also, it's up to you. Ok, so my 2x2x2 belongs in uFL. the below locations are where it is and how it needs to rotate. uFL: clockwise: M E M' E' counter-clockwise: E M E' M' uBR: clockwise: M E' M' E counter-clockwise: S' E S E' dFR: clockwise: M' E M E' counter-clockwise: S E S' E' dBL: clockwise: M' E' M E counter-clockwise: S E' S' E Also the 3 algs for double transpositions M slice: E2 M' E2 M S slice: M2 S M2 S' E slice: M2 E M2 E' These algs are all super short, and the intuition isn't that hard, they're all 4 move commutators. Wow this is cool! Chris
303. Re: [blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube] How come we let the cube decide... ?
From: "Thomas Kohn" <thomas.kohn@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 29 Nov 2005 11:23:14 +0100 (MET)

I ALWAYS solve with white on top and green in front, and i don't want to change to the the "new" method. i was thinking the following way: when i have white on top, i can have 4 colors in front, but the corner orientation is alway the same. if i had yellow (opposit of white) on top i have the same as with white on top. so i have only three possible possibilities to hold the cube (white, green or red on top). the sum of the corners that are to be oriented must be 8. ie: with white on top 4, green 3, and red 1. is that correct? so with white on top and 0, 2,3 or 4 corners to flip i can't get an advantage if i hold green or red on top. if 8 or 6 corners are wrong, it is better to take green or red on top and the new method is better. when 5 corners are wrong (3 correct) it could be that by holding green on top 5, 4, 3, 2, 1 or 0 are correct. but then (with red on top) 0,1,2,3,4 or 5 are correct. so only the first an the last 2 cases are an advantage. all in all, in 50% of all cases it is the best thing, to stay with white on top. let's say you need 3 seconds to see that green on top is better than white, then you need another 3 seconds to find the center permutation (ie EME'M') and 3 seconds to permute the center. that makes 9 seconds. how long do you need to flip 3 or 4 corners? i think less than 9 seconds. but now we did not yet talk about the edges. i think it will take too long to have a look at the edge orientation and you will gain nothing. that's why i still keep white on top and green in front. i memorise in 1:30 minutes (average) and try to be under 1 minute until german cube day. i think under 3 minutes is possible. memorise quickly and you have not the time to forget, solve quickly and you have bot the time to make mistakes! thomas kohn -- 10 GB Mailbox, 100 FreeSMS/Monat http://www.gmx.net/de/go/topmail +++ GMX - die erste Adresse f��r Mail, Message, More +++

305. Re: [blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube] Big cubes BLD - edges4x4 or wing edges5x5
From: Rob Butler <futuese@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 2 Dec 2005 07:23:55 -0800 (PST)

Hi Chris, Congrats on your progress on the 4x4x4. I too have the most problems with the edges on the 4x4x4 and 5x5x5 but practice and experience does definately make a huge difference here. I like to cycle my edges: UFl --- > ULf --- > URf --- > UFl using the following alg: F' dR'd'L dRd'L' F it might not be the easiest or the fastest but it is what I am used to and that counts for a lot. UFl is the slot that I work around so the two holes that I use every cycle are the ones on the left and the right faces. What I personally find to be critical on the edges is consistency in the set up moves. I estimate that up to 90 percent of my errors come while trying to UNDO the set up moves. Thus consisency is paramount. I try as hard as possible to place the first target edge into the left face and then the second target edge into the right face. Thus when it comes to undoing the set up moves I KNOW that I must undo the right face first and the left face second. Occasionally the way the set up moves go makes it really awkward to do it in this order. If this is the case then I set up the right face first and thus undo them in the opposite order but I consider it to be so EXCEPTIONAL that it is easy for me to remember to do things differently. I think it is also important to be consistant with your approach to the set up moves. There are often several different ways to set up a piece. Find a path that works for you to get each different piece to each different set up hole and then always use the same path. At first the set ups seem really difficult and complex but the more you practice the more options you will notice and the easier it will become. I also find it much easier to set up and undo set up moves while actually blindfolded than while just practicing with my eyes open. Less distractions from the other surrounding pieces I think. In sum. Consistency. Always set up the pieces in the same order. Always use the same set up moves. Always use individual slices and never use double slice turns. Once you are used to this it is just a matter of practice. Always be especially careful when undoing the set up moves. Best of luck Rob Butler --- cmhardw <foozman17@...> wrote: > Hey everyone, > > I have a question for the big cube BLDers. I've > been doing lots of > practicing still for 4x4x4 BLD, and I've noticed > that most often my > mistakes are actually executing the edges. For you > 5x5 or other 4x4 > people do you have any tricks? How do you 5x5 guys > execute the wing > edges? > > Also do the big cubes just take longer to learn and > more practice to > get used to before your accuracy goes up some? Just > curious what > others' experiences are. > > Thanks, > Chris > > > > __________________________________________ Yahoo! DSL Â¤ Something to write home about. 306. regular vs supercube 4x4x4 and 5x5x5
From: "Rob Butler" <futuese@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 02 Dec 2005 15:39:03 -0000

Wow, two posts in one day for me :) Yesterday I solved a regular 5x5x5 blindfolded. Yippie. What was really cool is that I actually made a mistake while cycling the + centers but was able to realize it and go back and correct it. Grace under pressure! I had previously solved a supercube 5x5x5 blindfolded because I had thought that it would be the hardest challenge out there and I wanted to go straight for it. Imagine my disappointment when the prevailing attitutdes started to shift towards the regular solves being more difficult. Well I have now blindsolved both the 4x4x4 and 5x5x5 as both regular cubes and supercubes. Personally I think that the supercubes ARE more challenging than the regular solves. Granted that the supercube tells you exactly where to place each center which can help to make the analysis easier. But parity solutions are easier on the regular cubes than the supercubes. And there are other advantages too. On the 4x4x4 you can choose how to start the cube regularly giving you 6 centers solved at the outset and frequently up to 8 centers already solved. That is 1/3 of the center cycle for free!! On the 5x5x5 the middle edge orientation and permutation is much simpler if you have already solved the centeres before doing them. The algs I use flip centers within a face and so must be used very carefully on the supercube but quite simply on a regular cube if the centers have already been solved. On the negative side the analysis is a little more difficult but not all that bad with a little practise. Cetainly not so bad as to outweigh the many advantages. At least in my opinion. Difficulty is in the mind's eye of the solver. For some maybe the supercube is easier. I just thought I would post that in my experience the regular solve is a little easier. It is a little bit splitting hairs however - to execute a 5x5x5 solution flawlessly requires focus and accuracy regardless of if it is a supercube or regular cube. Rob
307. Re: Big cubes BLD - edges4x4 or wing edges5x5
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 02 Dec 2005 21:29:10 -0000

310. Blind superprof parities - resent with correction of typo in alg !!
From: "Rob Butler" <futuese@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 03 Dec 2005 15:57:51 -0000

WARNING: LONG post and potentially a SPOILER. Do not read if you want to figure out your own solution to parity on the 5x5x5 supercube! Hi again Stefan, Here is my approach to fixing the parities while blindsolving the 5x5x5 supercube, or as I like to call it the superprof. The centercap / corners / midges / X center parity is extremely easy to identify and in fact is the very first thing I do. Simply analyze the 6 centercaps. If they are even there is no parity. If odd there is a parity. If odd the fix is very easy but it makes the analysis of all the data a little trickier. The fix is one you suggested for 3x3x3 about a year ago. I mentally perform either U or U' whichever is more advantageous. Parity solved but now I must be very careful to take this rotation into account while analyzing all of my cycles. The wedegs / + center parity is a little trickier. The only way I know for sure to discover it is to actually run through the cycle of the wedges. Theoretically it too could be corrected by a simple slice move (e.g.: u or u') but that would mean figuring out the whole cycle again and I don't want to do that after I have already gone through the trouble to memorize all of that data. So if I find a parity while analyzing the wedge cycle I will work with it. If parity is present than the cycle can of course be ultimately reduced to a single pair swap (considering only the wedges). After reducing the wedges to a pairswap I remember which edges need swapping and move on to the + center cycle. If there is a parity in the wedges there must also be a parity in the + centers which can also be ultimately reduced to a single pairswap. I have combined a pair of algs into a very long alg which will swap 2 wedges and 2 + centers while leaving the rest of the supercube unaffected. This long alg will: swap 2 wedges: UFl < --- > UBl and swap 2 + centers: UfM < --- > UbM It starts with an alg to swap the two wedges: [r U2] x4, r, [F2 l' B2 l] x2 But this messes up the centers so to put them back where they belong I use an alg which rotates the centercap 180 on a regular 3x3x3 supercube: [R L U R' L' U2] x2 The above alg fixes the centers in column l and column r but it rotates my 5x5x5 centercap 180 so I must repeat the above alg but with double slices to rotate the centercap back to solved: [(Rr) (Ll) (Uu) (Rr)' (Ll)' (Uu)2] x2. So, when combined the full and extended alg is as follows: [r U2] x4, r, [F2 l' B2 l] x2, [R L U R' L' U2] x2 [(Rr) (Ll) (Uu) (Rr)' (Ll)' (Uu)2] x2. Try it on a solved supercube and you will see that only the 2 wedges and 2 + centers are affected. It is a long process but it is not very hard to remember or execute once you are used to it. In fact I didn't even have to `learn' it at all since it is really just the regular parity alg I use combined with an alg that rotates a centercap 180. One long alg composed of two algs that I already knew well beforehand. One small detail to add. Since it is a real pain to keep track of 2 wedges AND 2 + centers while performing FOUR set up moves  I have a little trick to make life easier. While analysing the cube I have already established the presence of parity while memorizing the wedge cycle. Thus I know it will be present in the + centers before I start memorizing them. What I do then is to deliberately solve UfM into the UbM slot and UbM into the UfM slot. By introducing this additional pairswap into the cycle the rest of it can now be fully resolved leaving me with the two + centers swapped that will be fixed by my parity move. Essentially I alter the cycle to ensure that the 2 swapped + centers end up being the 2 centers that I want swapped. Thus I only need to worry about set up moves for my 2 wedges which poses no difficulty at all. Well this was a long post but parity can be complex and difficult to explain. I tried to explain not only HOW I solve parity but also WHY I solve it that way and how I identify it. I hope that it makes sense. Let me know if you need me to clear up any details. Note that on a regular 5x5x5 blindsolve the wedge / + center parity can be easily fixed by solving all the centers first and just using: [r U2] x4, r, [F2 l' B2 l] x2 ---- > many thanks to Masayuki for this alg !! Sure it will swap lots of X centers and + centers but on a regular solve  who cares. One of the reasons why I personally think that the superprof is harder to blindsolve than the regular prof (at least with my solution technique  perhaps your parity solution is much easier!) Yours, Rob

Hi Stefan, I realized that I didn't answer these questions in my parity post. > Re: 5x5x5 blindsolve - Congrats! What time? It took about thirty minutes to memorize and another half hour to solve. I just looked at a clock before and after I didn't use any timing device. > I'm also missing your super 5x5 time at speedcubing.com Yeah, I am pretty lazy about submitting times - I rarely time myself on blindsolves for big cubes. In fact I haven't submitted anything as of yet :( For the record I have no idea how long it took to memorize (I did it too long ago) but I seem to remember that it took about 45 minutes to execute the solve. While I am on a roll with posting - what alg do you use to orient midges on the 5x5x5 and the superprof?? My technique works but it is a bit of a pain. My alg is just a standard 3x3x3 two edge flip: M' U M' U M' U2 M U M U M U2 flips UFM and UBM But this unfortunately swaps the + centers in the M column on the U and B faces!!! No big deal on a regular solve - just do the midges after solving the centers! But this little trick wont work on a supercube. So for the supercube I flip edges mod 4 using this move - the first pairflip will swap the centers and the second pairflip will swap them back. If the edge orientation is not divisible by 4 then I solve the last two edge flips with: [M' U M' U M' U2, M U M U M U2, B2] x2 this flips UBM and DBM but is admittedly a bit of a pain to use. Do you have an alg that will flip midges without affecting the centers? If so it could be very useful to me. Also welcome would be a 4 midge flip since my algs will only flip 2 at a time. 312. Re: Blind superprof parities - resent with correction of typo in alg !!
From: "Stefan Pochmann" <pochmann@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 03 Dec 2005 17:44:25 -0000

I'll repeat Rob's warning: WARNING: LONG post and potentially a SPOILER. Do not read if you want to figure out your own solution to parity on the 5x5x5 supercube! Thanks Rob, very nice explanation of how you solve those parities. I tried the "start with U" fix for outer layer parity once and I think it was one reason why I failed. It forced me to think a lot and that's not good for me. I also thought about just memorizing two pieces swapped, but I never tried it. Before I show you my way, let me just show a possible replacement for your speedsolving parity fix. First part is the same but second part differs: [r U2] x4, r, U x' U' L' U r' U' L U r For me this seems easier to execute because it's only quarter turns and only <U,r,l,L>. Oh, and I just found out we have a nice self-correcting alg: [R L U R' L' U2] x2 I keep forgetting whether I shall do the U inside the first five moves and the U2 afterwards, or vice versa. Turns out it doesn't matter, the effect is the same: [R L U2 R' L' U] x2 Ok, now for my parity fixing. Actually I won't tell you exactly how I do it, but instead show you a cleaner version. Imagine you always "shoot" from certain U layer positions, e.g. UFl is always the first of the three positions of an outer edge 3-cycle (in reality I've used DLf). Do this for all piece types: outer edges: UFl middle edges: UFm corners: UFL X-centers: Ufl +-centers: Ufm Now when you end up with a single swap for a certain piece type, just leave it on U at certain places, e.g. leave UFl and ULb swapped for outer edges. If for example you end up having to swap UFl and RDf, simply do the 3-cycle (UFl->RDf->ULb->UFl), e.g. with the commutator [l D' l', U']. You only need to set up one piece and it's a very easy commutator. The "final swap partners" for the places mentioned above are just a U turn away, i.e. they are: outer edges: ULb middle edges: ULs corners: ULB X-centers: Ulb +-centers: Uls Just do this for all piece types. If there's a parity, append a 3-cycle at the end. This also means you don't need to detect parity beforehand. In case of center parity, leave it one U turn away from solved. Now let me just define a notation for conjugated commutators: {A:B,C} = A [B,C] A' = A B C B' C' A' At the very end, fix all parities like this: Outer layer parity: We want to swap the partners for corners, medges, +-centers, X=centers, and rotate the center. Do it in four steps: 1) { (Ll)' : (Rr)' (Dde)2 (Rr) , U } 2) U 3) [ l' , L' U' L U ] 4) [ L U L' U' , l ] Nice alg, easy to do in 12 seconds or so. I'll write it out and maybe make a diagram later. Inner layer parity: We want to swap the partners for +-centers and outer edges. Alright, gotta stop now and do some work, but I'll continue later. Or someone else could show an alg for this... Cheers! Stefan

315. 16 minutes!!!!
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 04 Dec 2005 04:55:17 -0000

Hey everyone, I got a 16 minute 4x4x4 BLD solve today and almost got the UWR too! The time was 16 minutes 39.61 seconds. I don't know how long memorization took me, since I didn't look, but I would guess about 3:00 minutes to memorize centers, 4:00-4:30 minutes for edges, and 0:45-1:00 to memorize corners. I try to be super careful on corners, so I think the total was about 7:00-8:00 on memorization and about 8:00 to solve. Man this is sooooo addicting! Now I really won't stop till I get the UWR ;-) Or at least get it until someone else beats it, which probably won't take long. I think my personal limits for this might be sub-10:00 minutes still. I can definitely learn to trust myself better for memorization and probably memorize centers and edges together in less than 6 minutes, then corners in 20 seconds if I practice more. Then I think I could learn to solve in less than 5 minutes if I practiced a lot. Well, I guess my goal is to get a sub-10:00 minute solve at home and on the couch, and just to get one successfully in competition. Man this is sooooo cool :-) I can't wait till I get more consistent and can consider the 5x5x5 as well. Chris

320. Re: Big cubes BLD - edges4x4 or wing edges5x5
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: blindfoldsolving-rubiks-cube@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 05 Dec 2005 20:37:49 -0000

Hey Rob, Thanks for the reply, I have been trying to take some of these tips into account when I solve after having read through it. > I like to cycle my edges: > > UFl --- > ULf --- > URf --- > UFl > > using the following alg: > > F' dR'd'L dRd'L' F > I like this type of commutator, I think I am going to start using them more often. I had never thought to do it this way before seeing you post this alg, thanks! My commutators are always of this form (or something based on this idea) [R' d R, U] > it might not be the easiest or the fastest but it is > what I am used to and that counts for a lot. UFl is > the slot that I work around so the two holes that I > use every cycle are the ones on the left and the right > faces. What I personally find to be critical on the > edges is consistency in the set up moves. I estimate > that up to 90 percent of my errors come while trying > to UNDO the set up moves. Thus consisency is > paramount. I try as hard as possible to place the > first target edge into the left face and then the > second target edge into the right face. Thus when it > comes to undoing the set up moves I KNOW that I must > undo the right face first and the left face second. > Occasionally the way the set up moves go makes it > really awkward to do it in this order. If this is the > case then I set up the right face first and thus undo > them in the opposite order but I consider it to be so > EXCEPTIONAL that it is easy for me to remember to do > things differently. I guess I want to ask to make sure, but do you always use that same alg to move the edges, and use setup moves every time? I am finding, that what is helping me to both get faster and more accurate for 4x4 (I have yet to try 5x5, so this might not apply there) is to use commutators on all faces, from any angle. There are cases where I used to use a setup move that now I can see that I can use a commutator from a different angle and have no setup moves at all. At first I lost a lot of accuracy since I wasn't used to doing commutators like that, but now I am getting used to it and I think I want this to be my approach in the future. I also want to learn commutators of the type that you listed above, I think broadening my reperotoire so to speak might make this approach mean I would hardly ever have to use setup moves at all, which is my goal. > I think it is also important to be consistant with > your approach to the set up moves. There are often > several different ways to set up a piece. Find a path > that works for you to get each different piece to each > different set up hole and then always use the same > path. At first the set ups seem really difficult and > complex but the more you practice the more options you > will notice and the easier it will become. I also > find it much easier to set up and undo set up moves > while actually blindfolded than while just practicing > with my eyes open. Less distractions from the other > surrounding pieces I think. > > In sum. Consistency. Always set up the pieces in the > same order. Always use the same set up moves. Always > use individual slices and never use double slice > turns. Once you are used to this it is just a matter > of practice. Always be especially careful when > undoing the set up moves. I also agree, lately I have been using the same style of setup moves (I do things on all faces, so it's just sort of a general trend) and I have noticed that sometimes if I forget the setup move I did, I can think of the position the pieces started in and think how I would set them up. This makes me recall the setup moves I actually did and I can still undo and get a sucessful solve. I also definitely agree to never use double layer turns, unless the double layer turn is your setup. Sometimes I can set up a very easy commutator to replace a hard one just by doing a double layer quarter turn, in that case I would use it, but other than that never. I guess my goal is more speed for the 4x4x4 and then maybe one day when I have perfected my approach to that, I will try to learn to speed solve the 5x5x5. You guys are crazy impressive to me with your attempts at difficult blindfolded feats. I guess I am more banal about it and just want to get fast at the 4x4x4, and one day of course try to expand to the 5x5x5. I don't really have any other plans other than just in my life getting one successful 6x6x6 BLD solve once they are sold online. Anyway thanks for the tips, and for opening my eyes to other commutators. I will definitely start using ones of that form more often now. Best of luck with your awesome BLD achievements, I'm still jealous about the 5x5x5 heh heh :-P Chris
